<div id="review_821006215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/821006215" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/821006215?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821006215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5387703795858282440">So basically I procrastinated reading this book FOREVER (because I'm a deluded pineapple) and <b>gosh, it was amazing and perfect and I <i>loved</i> it.</b>. The procrastination and fear it wouldn't live up to the hype were totally UNNEEDED. It's an epic retelling. So, so creepy and dark, which is <i>perfect</i>. I kind of reminded me a little of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12558285.Splintered__Splintered___1_' title='Splintered (Splintered, #1) by A.G. Howard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Splintered</a>. It took a fluffy old fantasy world (Oz) and TOTALLY messed it up. WHICH I JUST LOVE.<br/><br/>Although, to be honest, as I look at the gifs of the original movie, I kiiii</span>
  <span id="freeText5387703795858282440" style="display:none">So basically I procrastinated reading this book FOREVER (because I'm a deluded pineapple) and <b>gosh, it was amazing and perfect and I <i>loved</i> it.</b>. The procrastination and fear it wouldn't live up to the hype were totally UNNEEDED. It's an epic retelling. So, so creepy and dark, which is <i>perfect</i>. I kind of reminded me a little of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12558285.Splintered__Splintered___1_" title="Splintered (Splintered, #1) by A.G. Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Splintered</a>. It took a fluffy old fantasy world (Oz) and TOTALLY messed it up. WHICH I JUST LOVE.<br><br>Although, to be honest, as I look at the gifs of the original movie, I kiiiinda think it is creepy in a way too. I mean, come on? Tell me this isn't sort of terrifying:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428404259ra/14417109.gif" width="500" height="368" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>ANYWAY. Let's move on, shall we?!<br><br><b>Basically the book is about a girl, Amy Gumm, who gets sucked into a tornado and tossed into Oz...after Dorothy.</b> It's like the "then what happened story" of Oz. So wipe the idea of Dorothy returning home with her mini mutt. This story takes off with Dorothy being a sadistic ruler (with an affinity for the colour pink and glitter and fluffiness [which is terrifying]) of Oz. The Tinman and Lion and Scarecrow are all FREAKY. They torture people and do experiments and are just general not okay. Dorothy is a magic addict. She doesn't let anyone preform magic, because she wants it all. Glinda is psychotic. And everyone goes around with these botox like smiles.<br><br>Mostly the amount of fluffiness and pink in Dorothy's life, as she ordered people's deaths and what not, was what disturbed me.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428404259ra/14417110.gif" width="500" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>I love me a good retelling...and this is definitely a <i>good</i> one.</b> It was close enough to the original (well, it was set in Oz, after all) that I could see all the references. I felt like I was returning to a childhood story! AND it just turned everything from golden and shiny to dark, mysterious and creepy. LOOOOOVE IT. Good is bad and bad is good, how fantastic. (Although, to be honest, I think everyone was kind of bad?)<br><br><b>Amy Gumm is also fantastic.</b> She's a bit sassy and has foot-in-mouth, in that, she busts out with these caustic remarks that get her into a lot of trouble. I think she accepted the reality of Oz pretty fast, but, eh, we all have our daydreams, I guess. And I wondered about the fact that she never seemed to miss home or struggle with the scenery/reality change. But she was still fantastic and I loved reading from her POV.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428404259ra/14417111.gif" width="500" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>The romance?</b> Um...what romance?! It literally has like 3% romantic intentions. This didn't bother me AT ALL, except, towards the end, it kind of fished a relationship between Nox and Amy out of thin air. NO NO NO. It's <i>okay</i> to have a YA book without romance! IT IS. Forcing one in that doesn't fit just ruins things. I didn't ship anyone. It was all kind of weird and I felt zero chemistry between Nox/Amy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was also kind of weirded out that Ozma was masquerading as Pete. Um. Okay?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The plot was definitely interesting...if a little laggy in the middle.</b> We had to pause everything for a bout of magical training. *yawns* I was so not feeling it. I really think the book could've been SHORTER. Cut some of the laggy middle and exploration of Oz would've been more interesting to me.<br><br><b>All in all, IT WAS PRETTY DARN FANTASTIC.</b> It wasn't terrifying, but it was dark. And the sass was golden. AND ALSO FLYING MONKEYS. It was awesome to have fairly important non-human characters!! I LOVE FLYING MONKEYS.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428404259ra/14417112.gif" width="269 height=" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>YES I WOULD LIKE TO READ THE SEQUEL ASAP. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428404259ra/14417113.gif" width="500" height="208" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> (</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5387703795858282440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_900035361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900035361" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319681755p2/4605519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900035361?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4605519-jamie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900035361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10207664425820823100">I want to start off by saying that when I started this book I what I would think if it. My twisted sense of curiosity is what got the best of me on this one and I am glad it did. Lots of twisted and backwards adventure to be found here!<br/><br/>Amy Gunn is your average girl who has been dealt a bad hadn at life. She has no friends (thanks to nasty Ms. Madison), her father left when she was young and her mom is is a druggie. She wants nothing more than to get away from her crappy trailer life. Well she ge</span>
  <span id="freeText10207664425820823100" style="display:none">I want to start off by saying that when I started this book I what I would think if it. My twisted sense of curiosity is what got the best of me on this one and I am glad it did. Lots of twisted and backwards adventure to be found here!<br /><br />Amy Gunn is your average girl who has been dealt a bad hadn at life. She has no friends (thanks to nasty Ms. Madison), her father left when she was young and her mom is is a druggie. She wants nothing more than to get away from her crappy trailer life. Well she gets her wish; just no how she expected it.<br /><br />Welcome to Oz. But not how we know it. Yes the happy movies and the book is based on what <i>had</i> taken place but the story didn't end there...Dorothy came back and apparently became power and magic hungry. Glinda is a horrible slave driven, the munchkins are back to living in fear worse than with the witches. The beloved Scarecrow, Tin Man and Lion are mutated and twisted into something atrocious! And many other twists await!<br /><br />Let me give warning: DO NOT get attached to characters. There is a fair share of death in this book. And the first one I read has me very distrustful of bubbles right now and was gross! so unpleasant death at that! You have been warned...<br /><br />Then we get the fun job of attempting to figure out who to trust. Everyone tells Amy to trust no one. So that sends a firm message that has me wondering through the entire book. Many characters seem to have ulterior motives and secrets. So Amy has to train and learn to fight, control magic all while wondering what is going on and why.<br /><br />Danielle Paige has done a great job with character creation. Nox, Glamora, and other fantastic new characters are in this book. Amy I felt could have been a bit better. I do like her with her balance of flaws and abilities but her frame of mind and willingness so early on to kill disturbed me.<br /><br />The ending bit a bit rushed with lots of important facts but it is just sort of hurled at the reader. Which leads to my last small annoyance: the back cover is misleading....By the end of the book she is just barely starting on the actually missions set. When I got this book I was not expecting a long series. Now I wonder how long this can be. I have no problem with a series but I prefer my summaries to cover the book not the whole series arc. There is a lot if filler in this book. While enjoyable, it was not necessary and I feel is deliberately drawing it out (much like drawing a movie into 2 parts-I don't like that either).<br /><br />Less those few flaws, I really enjoyed this book. A good start to a new adventure. This is for older teens-adults with some graphic scenes and behaviors. The recreated world is fun to re-explore after many years. I will assuredly be continuing the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10207664425820823100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_900049576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900049576" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900049576?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=hate-the-heroine">hate-the-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=i-prefer-rum">i-prefer-rum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=abandoned-series">abandoned-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900049576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14654660944619972057">The rating would have been 2 stars higher if it had been a stand-alone with a proper conclusion instead of a rushed cliff-hanger and a confused protagonist.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416153973ra/11903429.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I don't feel like writing a proper review. Let's settle on why I did not rate it with 3 stars like I had expected around the first half of the book. <br/><br/><b>1.</b> The protagonist did not work for me. Like, at all. I get that she had a shitty life, I get that she is full of doubts and fears and repressed emotions, but usually when thrown into a challeng</span>
  <span id="freeText14654660944619972057" style="display:none">The rating would have been 2 stars higher if it had been a stand-alone with a proper conclusion instead of a rushed cliff-hanger and a confused protagonist.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416153973ra/11903429.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I don't feel like writing a proper review. Let's settle on why I did not rate it with 3 stars like I had expected around the first half of the book. <br><br><b>1.</b> The protagonist did not work for me. Like, at all. I get that she had a shitty life, I get that she is full of doubts and fears and repressed emotions, but usually when thrown into a challenging situation one either breaks or changes. Someway neither happened. Instead Amy continued to be her prior indecisive and defensive self and did not act unless pushed. <br>Which leads me to the next point, the <i>constant pushing</i>. I was annoyed around the second half of the book. In the first half Amy has to get used to Oz, I get it. But the second? <br>Nope. <br>Also, the clinging to the past was beyond annoying, Amy kept doing something I hated over and over again until I wanted to strangle her.<br>All in all, Amy seemed like an awful protagonist to me who was controlled by everyone and everything but not by herself. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386278879ra/7328408.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>2.</b> The pace of the book. After finishing it and looking up how many books are to follow I understood why the author wrote it this way, but understanding was all I did. <br>Fistly, it was slow. Much too slow. There was no action, there was no tension, instead the book felt like a steady flow to me, no rising and no falling. Which is a bad thing. For over hundred pages nothing happened. <br>At. All. <br>There was Amy struggling with Oz and its inhabitants and pages and pages of pointless, meaningless dialogue, but nothing else happened. Yeah, the pace was horrendous. <br>This usually goes hand in hand with a lack of atmosphere for me. Oz, the dark version of it, was <u>described</u> but not <u>shown</u>. Usually, I put up with it, but in this case I was displeased. I picked this book up hoping to get suck into a dark, gloomy world and found myself in a cheap attempt to copy Neil Gaiman. <br><b>Not good.</b> <br>Can you imagine a small pace with a complete lack of atmosphere? It does not sound very interesting, does it? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416155027ra/11903647.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3.</b> The dialogues, the world-building and the "plan". Okay, no spoilers here, but the solution of "the problem" was so terrible in my opinion that I nearly laughed. <br>Plot twists?? <u>Nope, not here.</u> <br>Surprises?? <u>Sorry to disappoint.</u><br>Not only was it stupid, but it was boring and painfully predictable. As was the outcome, really. <br>And as I have already mentioned, most dialogues were meaningless and served as page-fillers. But that's just my opinion. <br>Finally, the world-building. Or the lack thereof. Thanks to the dialogues and Amy's never-ending inner struggles and doubts the reader didn't get to see much of Oz, and in the cases Amy bothered with the world she was in she described it in about two sentences before going back to her approximately five thousand problems. <br><br>I have never liked the original tale, to be honest. And I did not like this retelling either. <br>Not recommended. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406650801ra/10578751.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14654660944619972057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950410733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1223485159910440829"><br/><b>
  <i>Well, I had wanted to be gone. I’d wanted it for as long as I’d known there was anywhere to go. I wanted other places, other people. Another me. I wanted to leave everything and everyone behind. <br/>But not like this.</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>We’re off to see the Wizard, the wonderful Wizard of Oz….</i>Is he, though? Is he really wonderful? And what about the rest of our beloved WOZ cast? Who’s good, who’s evil….and how do you interpret that little gray area in between? I <b>loved</b> this story and all the mayhem it represented. I</span>
  <span id="freeText1223485159910440829" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>Well, I had wanted to be gone. I’d wanted it for as long as I’d known there was anywhere to go. I wanted other places, other people. Another me. I wanted to leave everything and everyone behind. <br>But not like this.</i>
</b><br><br><br><i>We’re off to see the Wizard, the wonderful Wizard of Oz….</i>Is he, though? Is he really wonderful? And what about the rest of our beloved WOZ cast? Who’s good, who’s evil….and how do you interpret that little gray area in between? I <b>loved</b> this story and all the mayhem it represented. I <u>loved</u> seeing this new and intriguing twist on what was such a docile and somewhat sugar-coated version of evil in a faraway land, seeing what happens when power goes to your head and <b>no one can stop you</b>. What happens when little miss goody-two-shoes becomes the most violent and unforgiving ruler ever and….<b>did I mention this was violent</b>?<br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%2033_zpsk1mpe61d.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438606846ra/15733831.gif" alt=" photo giphy 33_zpsk1mpe61d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>Too bad they don’t have basements in trailer parks, I thought.<br>And then I thought: Bring it on. There’s no place like anywhere but here.</b><br><br><br>Omg guys, where do I even start? I’ve had this on my TBR for two years-<u>Two whole years</u>. When I first saw this splendid masterpiece of a cover, I was shocked-Evil Dorothy?? How could this be?!!! But alas, it was a year (or something) from being released and not enough people had read it-hell, I didn’t even have ¼ the friends I do now, so I had no one I could trust that had read it-I didn’t know who Khanh was, Emily May, or Wendy Darling, for that matter-I didn’t know <u>any</u> of the big names on GR. All I knew was that this was a twisted version of a beloved movie/musical/what-have-you, and I wanted to hop on board…<i>but was it any good</i>? I couldn’t be sure.<br><br><br><b>I didn’t know what was worse: to have your shot and screw it up, or to never have had a shot in the first place.</b><br><br><br>Years, obviously, passed and I forgot about it. I’d see it pop up here and there, but I’d be knee-deep in a buddy read or a super enticing series and I wouldn’t want to stop-so, again, I’d forget. And forget. And forget some more. But here I was, just scrolling through my feed a couple days ago, wondering what in the world I was going to read to break up my current series at the time (for some reason I’ve loved breaking my series up, lately-it’s been helping to keep me more excited/focused? I dunno lol), and then here it was, this beautiful cover attached to a very enthusiastic update about da boyz in the story…well, fuck me, it was like a light bulb went off over my head, the clouds parted, and the stars aligned…what more of a sign did I need?<br><br><br><b>The sky just overhead was almost black and the horizon was a washed-out, cloudy white, and I saw it, just like in the movies: a thin, dark funnel was jittering across the landscape and getting bigger. Closer. A low humming sound, like an approaching train, thrummed in my ears and in my chest. The lawn chair shot up into the air again. This time, it didn’t come back down.</b><br><br><br>What followed, naturally, was your typical Chelsea reaction to a wonderful and addicting book: Excessive smiling, giggling, hiding to find more reading time, general fangirling about my beloved Nox...the works. You know, the usual. There was just something so special about this book, something that <b>caused my heart to ache and my stomach to drop</b>-on more than one occasion. And, almost more appealing than anything, was the writing…It. Was. Perfection. Everything flowed seamlessly word for word and page to page-I was in heaven. And it’s became my favorite thing when a story doesn’t wholly center around the romance-well, not all the time do I want this, but when I pick up a fantasy or dystopian or action story, I adore the small, understated romances-and this was no exception!<br><br><br><b>
  <i>Who are you?</i>
</b><br><br><br>What I found here, instead of meaningless filler and forced conversation, was <i>substance</i>, something so often sacrificed these days. No, it’s not a story for everyone-the soul sucking, fear-eating Lion is testament to that. The only perfect animal character was my wonderful little Star, the Rat. Oh yeah, she took the place of Toto and I couldn’t have been happier with this little substitution! She was absolutely adorable and fierce-a completely loyal ally that had my heart melting time and time again. Don’t be fooled, though-this story has a lot of animals….But it was so much more than that. It was a story about a girl who grew up in less than desirable conditions, a girl who <b>starved for attention</b> and was a <b>social outcast</b> at school…only to find her purpose in a place known as Oz. The only problem? There’s already a girl from Kansas who’s had her life changed in Oz…and she isn’t willing to share. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/dorothy-satan-the-wizard-of-oz-favim-com-240165_zpsudfwdzhk.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438606846ra/15733832.gif" alt=" photo dorothy-satan-the-wizard-of-oz-favim-com-240165_zpsudfwdzhk.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>"They talk about Oz where I’m from. I’ve heard about it my whole life. But this is messed up. What happened here?”<br>Indigo’s impassive face twisted into a snarl. “<i>Dorothy</i> happened,” she said.</b><br><br><br><br>The cast in this story was beyond words. Do you even realize how fun it is to be reading about the villains? To see what they are willing to do to defeat the once good Cowardly Lion, Tin Man, Scarecrow, and Dorothy? Oh, and don’t forget about Glinda, the ‘good’ witch! Gone is the brainless Scarecrow, the heartless (but yet full of heart) Tin Man, the Cowardly Lion, and little Miss I-Took-A-Direct-Flight-From Kansas.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/the-wizard-of-oz-the-wizard-of-oz-gif_zpszq9zmdm3.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438606846ra/15733833.gif" alt=" photo the-wizard-of-oz-the-wizard-of-oz-gif_zpszq9zmdm3.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>They are unrecognizable in this story and I lapped it up, word by word-Especially when I saw that Dorothy went from girl-next-door to total voluptuous slut (And no, there really was no girl hate or slut shame! It was just a matter of fact when a girl didn’t like Amy or vice versa-no unnecessary bad mouthing-I know a couple girlies who don’t like that…). And speaking of Amy-What a remarkable and alluring character. I was utterly compelled by her determined attitude and willingness to do anything to help people she’d never even met before-all because she wanted to do what was best for a world corrupted by misused power. I loved her and my heart ached for her. <br><br><br><b>I didn’t know what was Good or Wicked anymore. All I knew was what was <i>right.</i></b><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/9182711_zpsqweboeo9.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438606846ra/15733834.gif" alt=" photo 9182711_zpsqweboeo9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>And then there’s Nox. Well, and Pete…but Pete wasn’t really a love interest-I just loved him all the same. Anyway-NOX. He really and truly didn’t have a huge part in this story, but when we met him, I was instantly in love with his standoffish, I’m better than you attitude. But, like many things, there was more to the story than meets the eye. He isn’t Amy’s biggest fan, right from the start-as he says, ‘Just because someone fell out of the sky doesn’t make them the one.’ He’s skeptical that Amy can take down Dorothy-and why wouldn’t he be? She’s just a small-town girl who’s never fought anyone. But don’t worry…it’s his job to train her ;). Did I mention I love fighter/soldier boys? Hmmm…<br><br><b>He just stared at me, his gaze intense. I couldn’t look away any more than I could move my arm. Energy crackled between us, and I felt a strange pull to him. Moth to flame. Magnet to magnet. Stupid girl to impossible, slightly mean witch boy. Wizard. Whatever.</b><br><br><br>It isn’t insta-love, insta-lust, insta-like…it’s more like a resigned acceptance that they have to work together. He doesn’t like her, and she doesn’t care for his attitude. But more and more <b>he begins to see her progress, and she begins to strive for his approval</b>. His begrudging admiration for her begins to blossom into protectiveness and concern, worry for what’s to come and if she’s really ready or not-but not once does he show it, making her think she is only a pawn to them all, including him…but she couldn’t be more wrong about Nox….and oh GAHD did I love seeing her falter in front of him, mistaking his concern for her safety for something entirely different-I am <i>such</i> a sucker for hidden romance, sigh. <br><br><br><b>Instead of looking down, I looked at Nox as he took in the landscape.<br>Seeing him like this, away from the caves, away from the cause, I could almost see the boy he could have been. The boy he <i>would</i> have been if Dorothy had never come back. He looked happy. He looked beautiful.</b><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mgtsm3y5hp1s04bf5o1_500_zpsomqrpien.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438607173ra/15733892.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mgtsm3y5hp1s04bf5o1_500_zpsomqrpien.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, I can’t seem to stop. And I don’t want to…but I will. I was so nervous I wouldn’t like this, but sometimes you are just in the perfect mood for something and it falls right into your lap. And lately, it seems, it’s getting harder and harder to do that-to find a book that just falls right in front of you that suits your mood. But I found it, and I am so so happy that I can start book two next weekend and that the final book is only a few month wait as opposed to a two year wait, like if I’d have read this when I originally wanted to. So, you see, <b>everything happens for a reason</b>. Amy has a new mission, a bigger purpose, more lies, deceit, and trust issues to overcome-who can she really trust in this gray world of wicked-wickeder-wickedest….I can’t wait for the battles, the young love, the misplaced trust and betrayals….but most of all-<b>
  <u>Dorothy Must Die</u>
</b>.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>Sometimes only pain can heal.</i>
</b><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>For more of my reviews, please visit:<br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

<div id="review_2014118771" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2014118771" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2014118771?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2014118771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3563527027584865379"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/>I grew up with the Oz books. As a child, I would revisit them periodically, curling up under the covers with a flashlight to read about Tik-Tok and the Wheelers, or Polychrome and the Nome King, or Mombi and Jack. Even now, I still occasionally read them because they're so fantastically creative and the imaginative world-building continues to hold up, even now. It's one of my favorite fantasy series ever, probably more so than Harry Pot</span>
  <span id="freeText3563527027584865379" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br>I grew up with the Oz books. As a child, I would revisit them periodically, curling up under the covers with a flashlight to read about Tik-Tok and the Wheelers, or Polychrome and the Nome King, or Mombi and Jack. Even now, I still occasionally read them because they're so fantastically creative and the imaginative world-building continues to hold up, even now. It's one of my favorite fantasy series ever, probably more so than Harry Potter. That's why I was skeptical when I saw that there was a series coming out that was a dark retelling of the Oz books.<br><br><br><br>DOROTHY MUST DIE is about a girl named Amy, who lives in a trailer park in Kansas. One day, she ends up being stuck in the middle of a tornado and, like Dorothy, finds herself magically transported to a world that clearly isn't Kansas anymore. It isn't quite Oz, either - at least, not the way that the fans know it. Everything is dark and drained of magic, and under Dorothy's corrupt rule it's turned into a Big Dorothy is Watching dystopia with torture, murder, and brain-washing all being totally commonplace. Welcome to Oz, b*tch.<br><br><br><br>To Paige's credit, the world-building is quite well done. I felt like the horrors really are that - horrific. The Tin Man, the Cowardly Lion, and the Scarecrow? All spectacles of terror that would be right at home in the jump scare-ridden world of Five Nights at Freddy's. I also liked the backstory about how Dorothy became evil. Power does corrupt and when magic is involved, that seems even more likely. Paige also portrays just how seductive power can be, even when it is evil, because in Dorothy's palace, things are beautiful, and it's all too easy to succumb to temptation.<br><br><br><br>Amy is one of those heroines I think people will love or hate. She's hilariously dated with her pink hair and emo attitude, like she's trapped in 2006 and nobody's told her that Green Day isn't cool anymore. She's also selfish and b*tchy and mean, with all kinds of snarky asides about pretty much anyone she doesn't like. She's not the villain of the story, though (yet?), and even though she's self-preserving she does risk her own life to save others at several points during the story even though cowardice or fear wins out a few times. I'm a fan of flawed protagonists, so this was refreshing; it's nice when women are allowed to be less than perfect in fiction and <i>still </i>be the heroines.<br><br><br><br>One thing about this book that I hated, <i>hated </i>is the long boring section where Amy trains with some witches to develop her powers and ends up meeting a boy named Nox. There's this weird sexual tension between them that feels awkward, because it's <i>so forced</i>, and I was annoyed to see bad-ass Amy lose sight of the game to obsess over some boy she doesn't even know. Seriously, at some point they pick up a wounded girl and Amy is <i>jealous </i>that he goes to attend her wounds rather than pay attention to her. Like, seriously, girl? Priorities, much? I'm thinking that there's going to be a love triangle between Pete and Amy and Nox, and I'm also thinking I'm not going to like it. Depending on how much focus this relationship takes in later books, it could be a deal-breaker.<br><br><br><br>This book, though, DOROTHY MUST DIE, isn't bad. As a retelling, it's decent. The writing is good and flows well (although it doesn't seem sure whether it wants to be a formal classically written fantasy novel or a breezy young adult narrative, and fluctuates wildly between the two styles). The author features characters taken not just from the Wizard of Oz, but <i>all </i>of the Oz stories (I'm hoping the Glass Cat will make an appearance; she was my favorite), which was nice. Even bitchy old Amy was a cool drink of water after the stale taste of too-perfect-to-be-true heroines I've been encountering in my usual YA fantasy line-ups, and that's definitely something we need more of.<br><br><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3563527027584865379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766347306?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=eye-roll">eye-roll</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=might-make-you-shit-bricks">might-make-you-shit-bricks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=ha-ha-not-funny">ha-ha-not-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=ending-sucked">ending-sucked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-am-not-pleased-with-that-cliffie">i-am-not-pleased-with-that-cliffie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=no-chemistry">no-chemistry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766347306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9259202469234427534"><a href='https://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402064697i/9889376.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>It's pretty obvious why this one was a must-read for me, right? A <em>Wizard of Oz</em> retelling where Dorothy is <em>evil...</em> I had to read it. No questions asked. And then I finished it... and was utterly disappointed. Remember my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926743760?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hexed</a>? I kind of felt that the writing in both books were similar, so if you enjoyed one you'll maybe enjoy the other.<br/><br/>So the story's told from Amy Gumm's perspective. Ah, Amy. <strong>The first word that comes to mind when I think of her is <em>shallow</em></strong>. She can't listen to any </span>
  <span id="freeText9259202469234427534" style="display:none"><a href="https://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402064697i/9889376.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It's pretty obvious why this one was a must-read for me, right? A <em>Wizard of Oz</em> retelling where Dorothy is <em>evil...</em> I had to read it. No questions asked. And then I finished it... and was utterly disappointed. Remember my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926743760?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Hexed</a>? I kind of felt that the writing in both books were similar, so if you enjoyed one you'll maybe enjoy the other.<br><br>So the story's told from Amy Gumm's perspective. Ah, Amy. <strong>The first word that comes to mind when I think of her is <em>shallow</em></strong>. She can't listen to any sort of advice or tips to survive, that girl. She just has to do the exact OPPOSITE of what other people told her to. Oh, and, there was this DYING girl--but she doesn't give a shit. She only cares that the guy she likes is tending to said dying girl.<br><br>Character development? Where!? All of the characters felt dry and one-dimensional. If they were developed to the slightest bit, they died and we didn't get more from them.<br><br>I did enjoy <em>Dorothy Must Die</em>'s concept. It's brilliant, right? I loved picturing the graphic descriptions regarding the Lion, the Tin Man and the Scarecrow... Oz is a creepy place and I would not want to live there. Despite the amazing potential the setting and plot had, I think the execution was kind of flat. <strong>Although there were the right amount of descriptions, I couldn't get a grasp of how Oz felt like</strong>. I didn't get the sense of a magical world with rich characters--rather, I felt like I was reading about a dry desert with a girl who lived alone. Everything just lacked substance for me.<br><br>What else--oh, yes. <strong>I didn't particularly feel like Dorothy was "evil" at all</strong>. She was just like some deranged attention-seeking bitch. And I definitely DO NOT appreciate how her character was portrayed as sort of a slut (a lot of cleavage was mentioned). Nope. Not how I picture an evil Dorothy at all.<br><br><blockquote>"For the Crime of Sass, This Monkey Is Hereby Sentenced to Official Attitude Adjustment. Do Not Tamper. By Royal Order of Princess Dorothy."</blockquote><br><br>Does that sound evil to you? No? Deranged bitch is more like it, right?<br><br>Wondering about the romance? HA. Insta-attraction, insta-jealousy--I can't even begin to describe how much this aspect bothered me. <strong>This is one of those books that do not need romance to make it interesting, okay</strong>?<strong> Nox, the love interest, was so boring and predictable</strong>. It was obvious that he would be the brooding love interest and that he would eventually like her back--a typical male lead. Nothing special at all.<br><br>This book did have those little details that I appreciated, hence my non-DNF rating for the book. For example:<br><br>&gt; Characters were realistic and betrayed one another to save themselves. We would probably do that to, if we're being honest.<br><br>&gt; Amy didn't magically turn into super-girl during tough situations. She was initially weak and admitted that a life-or-death situation wouldn't suddenly give her super strength.<br><br>&gt; There was a good amount of descriptions for me to picture the creepy and disturbing things the people of Oz have become. There was some action and gore as well.<br><br><em>Dorothy Must Die</em> was a waste of potential, if you ask me. So much could have been done with the book, but ultimately it lacked the flair I'm looking for in retellings of my favorite childhood stories.<br><br>---<br><br>In a nutshell:<br><br>Looking for a story to ruin your childhood and turn all you've ever known into something dark? Give this a shot. It's a book you'll either love or hate, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9259202469234427534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_773489935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773489935" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/773489935?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bubbling-under-5-stars">bubbling-under-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-m-your-barbie-girl">i-m-your-barbie-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=way-to-shoot-yourself-in-the-foot">way-to-shoot-yourself-in-the-foot</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer773489935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4837196776130683724"><b>EDIT 20/10/2014: Reason for change in rating in comment 9. My original thoughts on this book can be found below:<br/><br/><br/>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I've had my eye on Dorothy Must Die for a while now. Ever since the blurb came out, I've been eagerly anticipating the release because the premise sounds fucking fantastic. A dark retelling of The Wizard of Oz, an evil Dorothy and an assassination mission. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394200831ra/8820507.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My expectations were sky-high and Dorothy Must Die delivered.<br/><br/>Its world-building is on par with the likes of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12558285.Splintered__Splintered___1_' title='Splintered (Splintered, #1) by A.G. Howard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Splintered</a>, a </span>
  <span id="freeText4837196776130683724" style="display:none"><b>EDIT 20/10/2014: Reason for change in rating in comment 9. My original thoughts on this book can be found below:<br><br><br>4.5 stars</b><br><br>I've had my eye on Dorothy Must Die for a while now. Ever since the blurb came out, I've been eagerly anticipating the release because the premise sounds fucking fantastic. A dark retelling of The Wizard of Oz, an evil Dorothy and an assassination mission. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394200831ra/8820507.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My expectations were sky-high and Dorothy Must Die delivered.<br><br>Its world-building is on par with the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12558285.Splintered__Splintered___1_" title="Splintered (Splintered, #1) by A.G. Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Splintered</a>, a dark Alice in Wonderland retelling. But where Splintered failed with its over-the-top romance drama, Dorothy Must Die kicks blushing and feelings to the curb and focuses solely on the main point: opening a can of buttwhoop on Dorothy.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397978307ra/9353838.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Paige spares nothing in showing us just how dark and twisted this Oz is. There are no singing munchkins or serene Good witches. Winged monkeys cut off their own wings to avoid being enslaved. People are melted for not abiding to Dorothy's laws. The Scarecrow liquidates the brains of others to make himself smarter. And when people die, it's not quiet and peaceful with time to whisper a few broken words of encouragement to the heroine. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397978307ra/9353839.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's bloody and gruesome. The way wars are supposed to be.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397978307ra/9353840.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because this <i>is</i> war. Amy Gumm is just a normal girl living in Kansas, until one day, a tornado plops her in Oz. She's soon recruited by the Order of the Wicked to kill the tyrannical Dorothy and get Oz back to the way it was.<br><br>What I love about Amy is that she's tough, but holds the ability to be compassionate at the same time. She grew up in a trailer so she's used to taking shit from people. But she fights back when the time calls for it. She's not stupidly heroic or self-sacrificing for no good reason. She has a mission to do and she's damn well not going to screw it up for the sake of saving one person. She has <b>perspective</b>.<br><br>Yet that doesn't mean Amy is not good-hearted. When she first came to Oz, she freed a winged monkey from his punishment because she couldn't stand to see him in pain. She helps others when she can afford to. And when she fucks up, she <b>acknowledges it and learns from her mistakes</b>. Amy is a competent and sympathetic heroine, and I rooted for her even when her actions were morally wrong. You can't always stand from a moral high ground when you're a spy in enemy territory. You do what it takes to stay alive and complete your mission. That's it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397979031ra/9353919.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Also, I love the whole Good and Evil segregation. It reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16248113.The_School_for_Good_and_Evil__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___1_" title="The School for Good and Evil (The School for Good and Evil, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil</a>. What makes us Good and what makes us Bad? Is there no in-between? And when does "For the Greater Good" cross over the line?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397979031ra/9353920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's why the whole Dorothy-being-gorgeous thing didn't really bug me. It's a like a facade because like in the School of Good and Evil, 'Good' is always beautiful. Though I do think the makeover Amy gets while at the Wicked headquarters is largely unnecessary and only serves to further the romance. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394323654ra/8836597.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Speaking of the romance, that's the only complaint I have for this book. It could've been better played out and I never felt any real chemistry between Amy and Nox. It was like the author just stuffed it in because, hey, every YA book needs a romance. Props for good development though. And I'm probably going to be booed for saying this, but I sort of wish there had been <i>more</i> love-dovey time. A balance along the lines of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a> would've been perfect. Just maybe not the semi insta-love part. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397978307ra/9353842.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To wrap things up, Dorothy Must Die is a brilliant debut for Wizard of Oz fans and non-fans alike. If you loved the fantastical world of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12558285.Splintered__Splintered___1_" title="Splintered (Splintered, #1) by A.G. Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Splintered</a>, you will definitely enjoy what Oz has to offer. <br><br>Be warned that it's part of a series so it might read like of a set up for future installments. But a kickass one all the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4837196776130683724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_893387323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/893387323" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/893387323?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer893387323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17690361954591129292">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>3.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i> “Those who have sacrificed always have the most to lose”.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Amy Gumm has a pretty crappy life. She lives in a trailer park in BFE, Kansas, is being raised by a mother who is hooked on pills, and spends her days at school being bullied by a <i>pregnant</i> cheerleader. There’s not much to look forward to when she wakes up each morning. <br/><br/>Amy finds herself in a whole new world – literally – when her single-wide is swept up in a tornado</span>
  <span id="freeText17690361954591129292" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>3.5 Stars<br><br><b>
  <i> “Those who have sacrificed always have the most to lose”.</i>
</b><br><br>Amy Gumm has a pretty crappy life. She lives in a trailer park in BFE, Kansas, is being raised by a mother who is hooked on pills, and spends her days at school being bullied by a <i>pregnant</i> cheerleader. There’s not much to look forward to when she wakes up each morning. <br><br>Amy finds herself in a whole new world – literally – when her single-wide is swept up in a tornado<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/AWuJstd" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398954610ra/9487449.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(with less sharks)<br><br>and deposits her in the middle of Oz. But this Oz isn’t quite the same as the one Amy grew up hearing about. Dorothy and her gang are definitely a little <i>different</i><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/YmQ68jy" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398954610ra/9487450.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Okay, maybe not <i>that</i> different, but different in the fact that “words like <i>Good</i> and <i>Wicked</i> [have] lost their meaning” and the only thing that matters now is right and wrong. It’s up to Amy to determine who to trust (if anyone) and just how far she will go in order to save the land of Oz. Along the way she’ll cross paths with some familiar characters<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/F4dv8om" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398954610ra/9487451.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and get a helping hand from one or two unexpected allies<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/dzvHOV5" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398954610ra/9487452.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Growing up I loved old movies – especially musicals. Excluding two – “The Wizard of Oz” and “The Sound of Music”. Somehow both of these films have become “holiday classics” that I avoid like the plague. I can only assume it’s karma coming back on me for being pure evil. At this point in my life I’d rather stick a fork in my own eyeball than to have to watch Little Miss Goody Two Shoes (ha! I crack myself up) Dorothy traipse her way around Oz ever again. That’s why, when I heard of this anti-Dorothy tale, I <b>COULD. NOT. WAIT.</b> to get my grubby little hands all over it. And boy am I glad I did. Super fun, fast-paced, simply bubbling over with awesome. I really should be nice and give it a full 4 Stars, but I’m letting my inner-wicked-witch-flag-fly and bumping it down for two reasons: (1) I <b>HATE</b> books in a series and this one is so completely open-ended that I’m pretty much forced to read book #2; and (2) at some point authors have to realize that if they create a fabulous world filled with fantastic characters, they don’t need to muddy the waters worrying about who is going to be playing smoochy-face with whom by the end of the series. Just let the characters kick ass and take names.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17690361954591129292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3327565367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3327565367" />
    <a title="Maja  - BibliophiliaDK ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3444336-maja---bibliophiliadk"><img alt="Maja  - BibliophiliaDK ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588335087p2/3444336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3327565367?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja  - BibliophiliaDK ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja  - BibliophiliaDK ✨" href="/user/show/3444336-maja---bibliophiliadk">Maja  - BibliophiliaDK ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3444336-maja---bibliophiliadk?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3444336-maja---bibliophiliadk?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3327565367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8942508772584027222"><b>I WAS EXCITED TO GO BACK TO OZ, BUT GOT A DIFFERENT OZ THAN I EXPECTED</b><br/><br/>There were elements of this book that I really liked - the not knowing who was good and who was, the new role Dorothy was cast in and the main character Amy (in some instances at least) - and then there were elements I really didn't like. Was saddened me the most about this book was that it had such great potential, but for some reason I just didn't see it fulfilled. It wasn't a bad book and I think I'll finish the series all </span>
  <span id="freeText8942508772584027222" style="display:none"><b>I WAS EXCITED TO GO BACK TO OZ, BUT GOT A DIFFERENT OZ THAN I EXPECTED</b><br /><br />There were elements of this book that I really liked - the not knowing who was good and who was, the new role Dorothy was cast in and the main character Amy (in some instances at least) - and then there were elements I really didn't like. Was saddened me the most about this book was that it had such great potential, but for some reason I just didn't see it fulfilled. It wasn't a bad book and I think I'll finish the series all the same. It just didn't live up to my expectations.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Oz - where all your worst nightmares can come true."<br />- Amy</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>👍 WHAT I LIKED 👍</b><br /><br /><u>Ambiguity</u>: Who were the good guys and who were the bad guys of this story? I love that I can't answer that question. Amy, our heroine, is taken from Kansas by a tornado to Oz and falls right into the middle of a great power struggle with multiple sides, all claiming to be doing what's best for Oz. The fact that neither Amy nor myself could tell who were actually doing the right thing had me interested.<br /><br /><u>Amy</u>: I'll be completely honest, I don't love Amy. I went back and forth between liking her and being annoyed by her. I liked her when she showed sass and stood up for what she believed was right. I really didn't like her when she mooned over the mysterious Nox, who showed her little to no regard or affection. In the end I decided to give her the benefit of the doubt and list her among the things I liked. <br /><br /><u>Premise</u>: The idea of an Oz turned on its head because Dorothy had gone wicked was very intriguing. I only wish it had been executed a bit better.<br /><br /><b>👎 WHAT I DISLIKED 👎</b><br /><br /><u>Oz</u>: I remember both reading the books and watching the movie when I was younger and loving the whimsy of Oz, the magic and the characters. In this book I liked that the characters were so altered, but I was much disliked how much extra stuff was stuffed into Oz. It didn't feel like Oz anymore because so much extra had been piled upon it. If only Paige had kept to the tried and true Oz-mythology in stead of starting to invent her own, I would have been so much happier.<br /><br /><u>That special something</u>: I know this is really mean, because I cannot pinpoint it exactly - but I was missing something extra. That something, that made this one of those books, that I just couldn't put down. In stead, this was one of those books were I found myself skimming large portions of it because I just wanted to be done.<br /><br /><b>Follow me for more book loving content!</b><br /><a href="https://majaholmelund.wixsite.com/bibliophiliadk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ✨ <a href="www.facebook.com/BibliophiliaDK" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ✨ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/bibliophiliadk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/BibliophiliaDK" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br /><br /><a href="https://majaholmelund.wixsite.com/bibliophiliadk/post/12-kick-ass-female-characters" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog Post: 12 Kick Ass Female Characters</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8942508772584027222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1593725210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593725210" />
    <a title="catherine ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48622339-catherine"><img alt="catherine ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528240256p2/48622339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593725210?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="catherine ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="catherine ♡" href="/user/show/48622339-catherine">catherine ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48622339-catherine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48622339-catherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48622339-catherine?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48622339-catherine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593725210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer850277762358078162"><b>Actual Rating:</b> 5<br/><br/>Holy shit. This was amazing. <br/>Everybody take notes - this is the kind of story I want in a retelling.<br/><br/><i>Dorothy Must Die</i> centers around Amy Gumm, who is trash. Basically. Her father's left her, her mother is an addict, and she lives in a trailer in Kansas with no fun, no friends, and no future.<br/><br/>And then...a wild tornado appears! And it sweeps Amy and her little pet rat away from her boring and lame life. And they land in Oz. Except Oz isn't Oz. It's dark, it's barren, it's dirty, and </span>
  <span id="freeText850277762358078162" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating:</b> 5<br><br>Holy shit. This was amazing. <br>Everybody take notes - this is the kind of story I want in a retelling.<br><br><i>Dorothy Must Die</i> centers around Amy Gumm, who is trash. Basically. Her father's left her, her mother is an addict, and she lives in a trailer in Kansas with no fun, no friends, and no future.<br><br>And then...a wild tornado appears! And it sweeps Amy and her little pet rat away from her boring and lame life. And they land in Oz. Except Oz isn't Oz. It's dark, it's barren, it's dirty, and it's nothing like the fairytale land of sparkles and rainbows that Amy's grown up seeing.<br><br>So what happened? <b>Dorothy happened.</b> (Yes, our little blue and white aproned girl is the antagonist in this novel, and I love that).<br><br>Dorothy came back to Oz because she missed the magic, the power, the recognition. And she started to suck all the magic out of the land - <b>because she was hungry and greedy and wanted more than what she already had</b>.<br><br>And so, good is wicked, and wicked is good, and yet when Amy joins forces with the witches of evil (or good?) she must learn to harness magic and destroy Dorothy once and for all.<br><br>But of course, all is not what it seems, and of course, you never know who to trust.<br><br>Speaking in terms of plot, this was such a wild ride. It was full of action, adventure, and plot twists, and best of all, it was <b>believable</b>. Not believable as in "this is real, you have to believe me.", but believable as in "Silly reader, did you think that the story actually ended with <i>The Wizard of Oz</i>?"<br><br>The storyline was definitely full of surprises, and for me, I'd say it was an adventure from the very start - I was engaged from the moment Danielle Paige wrote about Amy's ninth birthday party.<br><br>Now, the writing style honestly wasn't <b>beautiful</b> or unique&gt; per se, but it was easy for me to get pulled in - and there <i>were</i> some scenes that made me go:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464793157ra/19277530.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>or just<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458505896ra/18496132.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, now my favorite part of this story was <b>definitely</b> the characters.<br>Amy was witty, sarcastic, and multifaceted - she had positive traits, but was not a Mary Sue, and she had flaws, but not annoyingly so.<br><br>The evil witches were kind but cruel and I trusted them and yet I was so suspicious - and it was impossible to decide and that's what made them great characters.<br><br>And Nox was oblivious and yet there were so many jewels and tiny moments between him and Amy - sometimes I wanted to smack him upside the head and other times I wanted to give him a big hug - and these are the crazy emotions that I want characters to make me feel.<br><br>And the characters that were originally in <i>The Wizard of Oz</i> became so wild and twisted - and yet they retained their original traits, <b>which is what a retelling should be all about</b>. And that is what I must applaud Paige for: for being able to keep bits and pieces of the original, and yet at the same time being able to make it entirely her own.<br><br>And no wonder I was able to finish this book not only in one sitting, but in the time span of only a few hours. Amazing read and I can't believe I didn't start it sooner.</span>
  <a data-text-id="850277762358078162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bf5gDHskIZxQlKO/C4FvgC3ySVjIwMCHkdzcN7wBi6JX2AnewHro9Pe/F978dGVf+62ukAZNTuDKopqGcUJ5OA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oc2USLEKHupoRad6AdVqlw43vY2A8E/4N3qHt37jLLab6/2aClTXgs9uExv2IGBI2GhaRU59wZ9sBMEGs6DeLA==')})
  }
//]]>
